Size and Industrial Distribution of Partnerships in 1936

A classification of partnerships for the year 1936 by size of net incomes and by industrial groups is presented in the accompanying table. This information was obtained by a special tabulation of the 1936 Federal income tax returns.1 Although partnerships are not directly taxable under the Federal income tax, they are required to report annually (Form 1065) their net income and the distributive shares of their individual partners. These shares are taxable to the partners under the individual income tax.2

Hitherto only incomplete official data have been available on partnerships. Statistics on the total number of partnerships (without classification by industry or size of net income) are contained in "Statistics of Income," compiled annually by the Treasury Department on the basis of Federal income tax returns filed. In addition, information on partnerships (a) with net income of $100,000 or

more, (b) with net income under $100,- 000, and (c) with deficits for the year 1935 was submitted to committees of Congress in connection with the hearings on the Revenue Act of 1936.

Partnerships with net income

The attached tabulation reveals that of the 230,004 partnerships covered, 87 percent reported net income in 1936. For partnerships the proportion of those reporting net income is more than twice as large as in the case of corporations. In 1936 only 38 percent of the corporations reported net incomes. Comparable data are not available for all sole proprietorships, but only for those reported on tax returns of individuals who had net income of $5,000 or more from all sources in 1936. Of this group 89 percent reported a profit from business enterprise.

In interpreting the fact that a greater proportion of partnerships

The study was sponsored and directed by the Treasury Department, Division of Tax Research, and financed by funds allocated to the Treasury Department under authorisation of the Commissioner of Work Projects.

2 The partnership return of income is an informational return; no tax liability is computed from it. Every domestic partnership, and every foreign partnership doing business in the United States or receiving income from sources within the United States, was required to file a return for 1936, the term partnership being defined to include "a syndicate, group, pool, joint venture, or other unincorporated organization, through or by means of which any business, financial operation, or venture is carried on, and which is not, within the meaning of this Act, a trust or estate or a corporation. . . ." (Revenue Act of 1936, section 1001 (a) (3).) The returns were submitted in original and duplicate to the several collectors of internal revenue, and unaudited duplicate copies were made available to the Income Tax Study for tabulation.

3 Hearings on the Revenue Act of 1936 before the House Committee on Ways and Means (page 428), and before the Senate Committee on Finance (page 20), 74th Congress, 2d session.

"The number of partnership returns used in the tabulation on which this analysis is based is approximately 97 percent of the number reported in 'Statistics of Income' for 1936, Part I." The data in "Statistics of Income" are based on a tally made in the field by the collectors of internal revenue from the originals of the tax returns. The omission of approximately 3 percent of the partnership returns from the present tabulation may be accounted for by (1) the failure of some partnerships to file duplicates of their returns from which the tabulation was made, and (2) the exclusion from the tabulation of those returns included in the collectors' count which, though filed in 1937, were neither for the year 1936 nor for fiscal years ending in the period July 1935 through June 1937.

5 Treasury Department, Bureau of Internal Revenue "Statistics of Income for 1936, Part 2", page 6.

than of corporations reported net income at least two factors should be noted. First, in computing net income, corporations are allowed to deduct the compensation paid to officers. Partnerships (and sole proprietors) are not permitted such a deduction. Second, the proportion of the total number of corporate returns represented by "inactive corporations" is somewhat greater than the proportion of the total number of partnership returns represented by "partnerships with no income data". Further, the deduction for interest may be less important for partnerships than for corporations.

Distribution by income classes

The heaviest concentration in the number of partnerships appears in the smaller net income and deficit classes. Two-thirds of the net income partnerships reported net income under $5,000. Less than 5 percent reported net income of $25,000 or more. Only 112 partnerships reported net income of $500,000 or more.

The concentration of net income firms in the class of less than $5,000 was paralleled by a concentration of deficit firms in the class with net deficits of less than $5,000. Of about 24,000 deficit partnerships, almost 90 percent were in that class.

Distribution by industrial groups

In 1936 two-fifths of all the partnerships were engaged in trade, chiefly retailing. Service enterprises,

including the professions, constituted the next largest group and represented 17 percent of the total. Financial enterprises comprised 11 percent and agriculture and manufacturing each approximated 8 percent of all partnerships. Among corporations, there was relatively less concentration in trade, and more in manufacturing and finance.

Partnerships with low net incomes and with small deficits were particularly numerous in some industries. In retail trade, 75 percent of those with net income reported less than $5,000 net incomes; 94 percent of those with net deficit reported less than $5,000 deficits. Similar proportions obtained in such businesses as domestic and personal service, automobile repair and garages, real estate, and farming.

In wholesale trade, in most branches of manufacturing and in the motion picture industry, partnerships tended to have an income larger than the average for all industries.

Although a partnership with a net income or a net deficit of $100,000 or more appeared in practically every major industry, most of the firms with a net income of $100,000 or over were either professional or financial in character. More than half were brokers, security dealers and law firms. Investment bankers, investment trusts, and accountants were also numerous in the higher net income groups.

Similar data for corporations and sole proprietorships are contained in "Statistics of Income".

See footnote 2, page 1. The industrial classification adopted is that which is being used by the Bureau of Internal Revenue for sole proprietorships for the taxable year 1936. This classification comprises 9 industrial divisions divided into 55 major industrial groups, which are in turn subdivided into minor groups. Not all the major or minor groups are distinguished in the table. The partnership return for 1936, Form 1065, provided a space in which the type of business or profession was to be indicated, and in the majority of cases the industrial classification of returns was made from this statement. In instances where two or more business activities were indicated on a return an attempt was made to determine the predominant activity in terms of gross receipts. Where the several activities indicated were within one industrial division, but the predominant group could not be determined, the return was assigned to a classification for returns not definitely allocable to a specific group within the division. Returns for which the kind of business was not given are shown in the non-allocable division.

The amount reported for net income prior to the distribution of income among the partners was used in classifying returns by size of net income. This figure was accepted as it appeared on the return without adjustment, except in cases where it could be determined that withdrawals of partners had been erroneously deducted.

4/ Includes (1) other agriculture and related industries and (2) agriculture and related industries not allocable to a major group.
5/ Includes 3,192 returns of owned oil and gas companies which give no net income data. These returns were filed in compliance with Income Tax Unit decision 2749.
6/ Includes (1) communication and related services, (2) public utilities not elsewhere classified and, (3) public utilities not allocable to a major group.
7/ Includes (1) other personal service and (2) domestic and personal service not allocable to a minor group.
8/ Includes (1) adjustment and credit bureaus and collecting agencies; (2) private employment agencies; (3) duplicating, addressing, blue- printing, photostating, mailing, and mailing list services; (4) business services not elsewhere classified; and (5) business services not allocable to a minor group.
9/ Includes (1) amusement, recreation, and related services other than motion pictures and (2) amusements not allocable to a minor group.
10/ Includes (1) businesses reported on returns which do not fall within preceding industrial divisions and (2) all other returns with kind of business not stated.

Sotel The amount of customs duties and taxes is calculated on the basis of reports of the Bureau of Foreign and Domestic Commerce, showing the quantity and value of merchandise imported. 1/ Figures are rounded to nearest thousand, and will not necessarily add to totals. 2/ Includes taxable sugar from the Philippine Islands. 3/ Duty-free commodities taxed under the Revenue Act of 1932 and subsequent acts. 4/ Articles dutiable under paragraph 1615 and repairs on vessels dutiable under Section 466 of the Tariff Act of 1930; the taxable copper content of dutiable articles taxed under the Revenue Act of 1932 and taxes on articles composed in chief value of manufactured sugar under the Sugar Act of 1937, which cannot be allocated to appropriate schedules. Taxes collected on other dutiable commodities under the revenue acts and the Sugar Act of 1937 are included in appropriate schedules.

Net Capital Movement between the United States and Foreign Countries
